--- Message (Timothy Day, 2025-02-18 17:20:11.000000000) ---

> Patch Set 5:

--- Message (Patrick Farrell, 2025-02-18 17:24:57.000000000) ---
Patch Set 5:

I really think we can do it with checkpatch - it's what we've done before.

We could screw it up, but that's always possible.

--- Message (Timothy Day, 2025-02-18 19:08:20.000000000) ---
Patch Set 5:

> Patch Set 5:
> 
> I really think we can do it with checkpatch - it's what we've done before.
> 
> We could screw it up, but that's always possible.

To be precise, I'm talking about preventing the use of the folio compat APIs [1]. Matt Wilcox called out those APIs in particular.

If we know for certain that some APIs will be replaced/removed, it's seems ideal to discourage usage as soon as possible. Eventually, the kernel itself will remove these folio compat APIs. So if we can get Lustre strictly deprecate them beforehand, it will save us a lot of effort down the line. I think a compile time check will be followed more strictly than a checkpatch warning. People writing new code with old APIs could cause a lot of wasted effort that we could avoid.

I agree that we should start with checkpatch. But I guess I don't see any downside to a stricter check?

[1] https://elixir.bootlin.com/linux/v6.14-rc3/source/mm/folio-compat.c

--- Message (Shaun Tancheff, 2025-02-28 06:15:03.000000000) ---
Patch Set 8:

> Patch Set 8:
> 
> (3 comments)
> 
> What will be our ability to allocate large folios (e.g. 1MB+) for cases when clients are doing large streaming read/write operations?  Will this get us there, or this is just plumbing in the the basic APIs and more work still needed?

Eventually yes. From el9.5 and any 6.11 kernel we just flag the mapping with the maximum order we can handle and on each write_begin() we set the size of the I/O [ideally aligned with the stripe so we do not have to deal with a lot of truncated/split folios].

> 
> No pressure, I'm just trying to understand these changes better?
